	%\xdbheadrightarrow
	
	\title{Grothendieck topology of  $C^*$-algebras}
	
	\author
	{\textbf{Petr R. Ivankov*}\\
		e-mail: * monster.ivankov@gmail.com \\
	}
	
	\begin{document}

\maketitle  %\setlength{\parindent}{0pt}
\pagestyle{plain}


%\vspace{1 in}


%\noindent

\begin{abstract}
For any topological space there is a sheaf cohomology. A Grothendieck topology  is a generalization  of the  classical topology such that  it also possesses a sheaf cohomology. On the other hand any noncommutative $C^*$-algebra is a generalization of a locally compact Hausdorff space. Here we define a Grothendieck topology arising from  $C^*$-algebras which is a generalization of the topology of the spectra of commutative $C^*$-algebras. This construction yields a noncommutative generalization of the sheaf cohomology of topological spaces.  The presented here theory gives a unified approach to  the  Gelfand duality and the duality between the commutative von Neumann algebras and measure locales.  The generalization of the  Dixmier-Douady theory  concerning $C^*$-algebras of foliations is also discussed.  

\end{abstract}


%\end{abstract}

\section{Gelfand topoi}
\subsection{Grothendieck topology}\label{groth_top_sec}
\begin{definition}\label{hered_cat_defn}
If $A$ is a $C^*$-algebra then there is a category $\mathbf{Hered}/A$ such that:
\begin{itemize}
	\item $\mathbf{Hered}/A$-objects are hereditary $C^*$- subalgebras of $A$,
	\item $\mathbf{Hered}/A$-morphism  from $B' \subset A$ to $B'' \subset A$ is a natural inclusion $B''\subset B'$ such that a following diagram 
	\newline
	\begin{tikzpicture}
		\matrix (m) [matrix of math nodes,row sep=3em,column sep=4em,minimum width=2em]
		{
			B'  &  & B''\\ 
			& A &\\};
		\path[-stealth]
		(m-1-1) edge node [above] {$\supset$} (m-1-3)
		(m-2-2) edge node [above]  {} (m-1-1)
		(m-2-2) edge node [right]  {} (m-1-3);
	\end{tikzpicture}
	\\
	is commutative. In the above diagram the morphism $A \to B'$ and $A \to B'$  correspond to inclusions $B' \subset A$ and $B'' \subset A$.
\end{itemize}
Note that the trivial $C^*$-algebra is a final object of the category.
\end{definition}
\begin{definition}\label{pullback_covering_ca_defn}
	For any two $\mathbf{Hered}/A$-objects $B', B''$ we define their \textit{fibre product} or \textit{pullback} (cf. Definition \ref{pullback_defn}) by the following way
\be\label{fibre_eqn}
B'\times_{\{0\}} B'' \bydef   \quad \text{ a generated by }\quad  B'\cup B'' \quad \text{hereditary subalgebra of } \quad A.
\ee
$\mathbf{Hered}/A$.
\newline
\begin{tikzcd}
B'\times_{\{0\}} B'' \arrow[d] \arrow[r]
	& B''\arrow[d, ""]\\
B'\arrow[r, ""]	& \{0\}
\end{tikzcd}

	For any $\mathbf{Hered}/A$-object $B$ a distinguished set of families of morphisms $\left\{B_\iota \to B\right\}_{\iota=1,..,n}$, called a \textit{covering} of $B$ if $\bigcap_{\iota=1}^n B_\iota = B$. Recall that morphism any $B'\to B''$ is an inclusion $B'' \subset B'$. 
	\end{definition} 
	
	\begin{theorem}\label{ca_site_thm}
	The Definition \ref{pullback_covering_ca_defn} yields a Grothendieck pretopology (cf. Definition \ref{pretopology_defn}).
	\end{theorem}
	\begin{proof}
	One needs check conditions (a) - (c) of the Definition \ref{pretopology_defn},\\
	(a) If $B$ and $C$ are $\mathbf{Hered}/A$-objects such that there is a morphism $C \to B$ then $B \subset C$. Moreover $B\times_{\{0\}} C= C$. If $\left\{B_\iota \to B\right\}_{\iota= 1,...,n}$ is a covering of $B$  then $B = \bigcap_{\iota 1}^n B_\iota$. Moreover $B\times_{\{0\}} C= C$. 
	From 	
	$$
	C = 	B \cup C = \left( \bigcap_{\iota \in 1}^n B_\iota \right) \cup C = \bigcap_{\iota =1}^n\left( B_\iota\cup C\right) 
	$$
	it follows that the family $\left\{ B_\iota\cup C\right\}_{\iota =1,...,n}$ is a covering of $C$.\\
	(b) If $B = \bigcap_{\iota 1}^n B_\iota$ and $B_\iota =  \bigcap_{j 1}^{n_\iota}B_{\iota,j}$ for all $\iota \in I$ then $B = \bigcap_{\iota, j} B_{\iota,j}$.\\
	(c) Evident.
	\end{proof}
	


\begin{definition}\label{gelfand_a_site_defn}
	The given by the Theorem \ref{ca_site_thm} site (cf. Definition \ref{grotendieck_topolgy_defn}) $\mathbf{T}_A\bydef \left(\mathbf{Hered}/A, J_A\right)$ is said to be \textit{Gelfand}  $A$-\textit{site} (cf. Definition \ref{top_gro_definition}). The topology $J_A$ is said to be the \textit{Gelfand} $A$-\textit{topology}. We use the following notation
	\be\label{a_site_eqn}
\mathfrak{Site}\left(A \right)\bydef \mathbf{T}_A.
	\ee
	  A  topos 
	\be\label{a_topos_eqn}
	\mathfrak{Topos}\left( A\right)  = \mathbf{Sh}\left(\mathbf{T}_A \right). 
	\ee	
	which is a category of sheaves over the site $\mathfrak{Site}\left(A \right)$ is said to be the \textit{Gelfand} $A$-\textit{topos}. 
\end{definition}
\begin{lemma}\label{site_lim_lem}
The described above category $\mathbf{Hered}/A$ has finite limits.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
From the Proposition \ref{fin_lim_prop} one needs check that 	has a terminal object and pullbacks. The terminal object is a trivial $C^*$-algebra $\{0\}$, pullbacks are given by the equation \eqref{fibre_eqn}.
\end{proof}

\begin{notation}\label{hom_ring_not}
 Similarly to the Definition \ref{forget_sheaf_defn} the Remark \ref{ab_uss_rem} the following notation will be used:
\be\label{sheaf_notation_eqn}
\begin{split}
	\mathbf{PreSh}\left(A\right)\bydef	\mathbf{PreSh}\left(\mathbf{T}_{A} \right) 	\cong 	\mathbf{PreSh}\left(\mathbf{T}_{\mathfrak{Site}\left(A \right)} \right),\\
\mathbf{Sh}\left(A\right)\bydef	\mathbf{Sh}\left(\mathbf{T}_{A} \right) \cong 	\mathbf{Sh}\left(\mathbf{T}_{\mathfrak{Site}\left(A \right)} \right),\\
\mathbf{PreAb}\left(A\right)\bydef	\mathbf{PreAb}\left(\mathbf{T}_{A} \right) \cong 	\mathbf{PreAb}\left(\mathbf{T}_{\mathfrak{Site}\left(A \right)}\right),\\
\mathbf{Ab}\left(A\right)\bydef	\mathbf{Ab}\left(\mathbf{T}_{A} \right) \cong 	\mathbf{Ab}\left(\mathbf{T}_{\mathfrak{Site}\left(A \right)}\right)
\end{split}
\ee
The trivial subalgebra $\{0\}\subset A$ if the terminal object of $\mathbf{Hered}/A$ for  any sheaf $\mathscr F \in \mathbf{Ab}\left(A\right)$ and/or presheaf $\mathscr P \in \mathbf{PreAb}\left(A\right)$ of Abelian groups the following notation is used
\be\label{cohom_sheaf_not}
\begin{split}
H^r\left(\mathfrak{Site}\left(A \right),\mathscr F\right)\bydef H^r\left(\{0\},\mathscr F\right),\\
\check H^r\left(\mathfrak{Site}\left(A \right),\mathscr P\right)\bydef \check H^r\left(\{0\},\mathscr P\right),\\
\end{split}
\ee
where $r \ge 0$ (cf. equations \eqref{etale_coh_eqn} and \eqref{cech_hom_comp_eqn} respectively).
If $F$ is an Abelian group and $F_{\mathbf{Hered}/A}$ (resp. $F_{\mathfrak{Site}\left(A \right)}$) is a constant presheaf (resp. sheaf) then for any $r > 0$ we use the following notation
\bea\label{hom_eqn}
H^r\left(\mathfrak{Site}\left(A \right),F\right)\bydef  {H}^r\left(\mathfrak{Site}\left(A \right), F_{\mathfrak{Site}\left(A \right)} \right),\\
\label{chech_hom_eqn}
\check H^r\left(\mathfrak{Site}\left(A \right), F\right)\bydef\check{H}^r\left(\mathfrak{Site}\left(A \right), F_{\mathbf{Hered}/A} \right) \cong \check{H}^r\left(\mathfrak{Site}\left(A \right), F_{\mathfrak{Site}\left(A \right)} \right).
\eea
If $R$ is a ring then there is a graded ring 
\be\label{cohom_ring}
\check H^\bullet\left(\mathfrak{Site}\left(A \right), R\right)
\ee
(cf. the Lemma \ref{gr_ring_lem}, and the Remark \ref{ring_homo_rem}).
\end{notation}

%\begin{lemma}\label{min_lem}
%Let $A$ be a $C^*$-algebra, and let $B$ be a hereditary $C^*$-subalgebra of $A$. %\end{lemma}

\subsection{Geometric morphisms}

\begin{definition}\label{hereditary_full_defn}
If both be $A$ and $\widetilde{A}$ be $C^*$-algebras then  a ring homomorphism of $\C$-algebras
\bean
\varphi_R: A \hookto \mathbf{RC}\left(\widetilde A\right)
\eean
(where $\mathbf{RC}\left(\widetilde A\right)$ is a space of right centralizers cf. Definition \ref{lrc_defn}) is said to be a \textit{hereditary full} if 
\begin{itemize}
	\item  a left ideal $\widetilde{A} \varphi\left(A \right)$  is dense in $\widetilde{A}$,
	\item 
	$$
	\forall a \in A \quad \left\|\varphi_R\left( a \right)  \right\|_{\mathbf{RC}\left(\widetilde A\right)} \le  \left\|a \right\|_{A}
	$$
	where both $\left\|\cdot  \right\|_{\mathbf{RC}\left(\widetilde A\right)}$ and $\left\|\cdot  \right\|_{A}$ are the natural norm on $\mathbf{RC}\left(\widetilde A\right)$ and the $C^*$-norm on $A$.
\end{itemize}
Similarly $\varphi_L: A \hookto \mathbf{LC}\left(\widetilde A\right)$  is said to be a \textit{hereditary full} if  a right ideal $ \varphi\left(A \right)\widetilde{A}$  is dense in $\widetilde{A}$.

\end{definition}
If	$\varphi: A \hookto \mathbf{LC}\left(\widetilde A\right)$ be a {hereditary full} morphism then there is a functor
\be\label{geom_functor_eqn}
\begin{split}
	\overline \varphi : \mathbf{Hered}/A \to \mathbf{Hered}/\widetilde A ,\\
B \mapsto C^*\text{-norm completion of } \varphi\left(B \right)^*\widetilde{A} \varphi\left(B \right). 
\end{split}
\ee
\begin{theorem}\label{geometric_morphism_thm}
The functor \eqref{geom_functor_eqn} yields a  morphism of sites 
\be\label{site_morphism_eqn} 
\mathfrak{Site}\left( \widetilde A \right) \xrightarrow{\mathfrak{Site}(\varphi)}\mathfrak{Site}\left( A\right) 
\ee
(cf. Definition \ref{morphism_of_sites_defn}). There is a natural geometric morphism
\be\label{geometric_morphism_eqn} 
\mathfrak{Topos}\left( \widetilde A \right) \xrightarrow{\mathfrak{Topos}(\varphi)}\mathfrak{Topos}\left( A\right) 
\ee
(cf. Definition \ref{geometric_morphism_defn})
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
From the Lemma \ref{site_lim_lem} it follows that both categories $\mathbf{Hered}/A$ and $\mathbf{Hered}/\widetilde A$ have finite limits. According to the Definition  \ref{morphism_of_sites_defn} one needs check the given by \eqref{geom_functor_eqn} functor $\overline \varphi$ satisfies to the following conditions:
\begin{enumerate}
	\item[(i)] $\overline \varphi$ preserves finite limits,
	\item[(ii)] $\overline \varphi$ preserves coverings
\end{enumerate}
A  proof of these conditions is left to the reader. The existence of the geometric morphism \eqref{geometric_morphism_eqn} follows from the Theorem \ref{site_mor_thm}/ 
\end{proof}
\begin{empt}
		Let both $\left(\mathbf{C}, J\right)$ and $\left(\mathbf{D}, K\right)$  are two sites, and suppose that $\phi:\mathbf{C}\to \mathbf{D}$ satisfies to the Definition \ref{morphism_of_sites_defn}. From the Theorem \ref{site_mor_thm} it follows that there is a geometric morphism  $\mathbf{Sh}\left(\mathbf{D}, K\right)\xrightarrow{f} \mathbf{Sh}\left(\mathbf{C}, J\right)$. A following lemma is an analog of (i) of the Proposition \ref{spectral_sequence_prop}
		\end{empt}

\begin{lemma}\label{cech_geom_lem}
In the above situation if $\mathscr A\in \mathbf{Ab}\left(\mathbf{D}, K\right)$ then for all $r \ge 0$ we have a homomorphism of \v{C}ech cohomology
$$
\check H^r\left(\mathbf{Sh}\left(\mathbf{C}, J\right), \mathscr A \right) \to \check H^r\left(\mathbf{Sh}\left(\mathbf{D}, K\right), f^*\mathscr A \right)
$$
(cf. Definition \ref{cech_defn})
where $f^*$ is the inverse image of the geometric morphism $\mathbf{Sh}\left(\mathbf{D}, K\right)\xrightarrow{f} \mathbf{Sh}\left(\mathbf{C}, J\right)$.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
	From the proof of the Statement  \ref{associated_sheaf_stmnt} it follows that for any $\mathbf{C}$-object $U$ there is a homomorphism  $\phi_U:\mathscr A\left(U \right)  \to  f^*\mathscr A\left(\phi\left( U\right)  \right)$. For any covering $\mathscr U$ of $\mathbf{C}$ there is the natural covering $\phi \mathscr U$ of $\mathbf{D}$. If
	$$
	s\bydef  C^r\left( \mathscr U, \mathscr A\right)
	$$
	is a chain (cf. \eqref{chech_eqn} then  one has a natural chain 
	$$
\phi^*s \in  C^r\left(\phi \mathscr U, f_*\mathscr A\right)
	$$
For $s \in C^r\left( \mathscr U, \mathscr P\right)$  one has
\bean
d^rs_{\iota_0,..., \iota_{r + 1}}\bydef \sum_{j = 0}^{r + 1}\left(-1 \right) \mathrm{res}_j\left(s_{\iota_0,..., \iota_{j-1},\iota_{j+1},..., \iota_{r + 1}} \right). 
\eean 
It follows that
\be\label{diff_phi_eqn}
\begin{split}
d^r \phi^*s_{\iota_0,..., \iota_{r + 1}}\bydef \sum_{j = 0}^{r + 1}\left(-1 \right) \mathrm{res}_j\left(\phi^*s_{\iota_0,..., \iota_{j-1},\iota_{j+1},..., \iota_{r + 1}} \right),\\
d^r s = 0 \quad  \Rightarrow \quad d^r \phi^*s= 0,\\
s \in \im ~d^{r-1} \quad  \Rightarrow \quad \phi^*s \in \im~ d^{r-1}
\end{split}
\ee
From \eqref{diff_phi_eqn} there is a homomorphism
$$
\check H^r\left( \mathscr U, \mathscr A\right)\to \check  H^r\left( \phi \mathscr U,f^* \mathscr A\right)
$$
From the homomorphism $\check H^r\left( \phi \mathscr U,f^* \mathscr A\right)\to \check  H^r\left(\mathbf{Sh}\left(\mathbf{D}, K\right), f^*\mathscr A \right)$ one has a homomorphism
$$
\check H^r\left( \mathscr U, \mathscr A\right)\to \check H^r\left(\mathbf{Sh}\left(\mathbf{D}, K\right), \mathscr A \right)
$$
Taking into account that $\check H^r\left(\mathbf{Sh}\left(\mathbf{C}, J\right), A\right)  \mathscr\bydef \varinjlim_{\mathscr U}\check H^r\left( \mathscr U, \mathscr A\right)$ we obtain the required homomorphism $\check H^r\left(\mathbf{Sh}\left(\mathbf{C}, J\right), \mathscr A \right) \to \check H^r\left(\mathbf{Sh}\left(\mathbf{D}, K\right), f^*\mathscr A \right)$.
\end{proof}



\section{Topoi of commutative $C^*$-algebras}
\subsection{Sites}\label{top_closed_sec}
\paragraph{}
Let $\sX$ be a locally compact, Hausdorff topological space, and let $A \bydef C_0\left( \sX\right)$ be a corresponding commutative $C^*$-algebra. Any hereditary $C^*$-subalgebra $B \subset A$ is an closed ideal which uniquely depends  an open subset
\be\label{top_xb_eqn}
\sX_B \bydef\left\{x \in \sX\quad |\quad \exists a \in B \quad a\left(x \right)= 0\right\}.
\ee

The category $\mathbf{Hered}/C_0\left(\sX \right)$ is equivalent to the category $\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right)$ such that:
\begin{enumerate}
	\item[(i)] $\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right)$-objects are closed subsets of $\sX$.
	\item[(ii)] $\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right)$-morphisms are natural inclusions of closed subsets
	\newline
\begin{tikzpicture}
	\matrix (m) [matrix of math nodes,row sep=3em,column sep=4em,minimum width=2em]
	{
	\sU' & &\sU''	\\ 
	&\sX &	\\};
	\path[-stealth]
	(m-1-1) edge node [below]  {$\subset$} (m-1-3)
	(m-1-1) edge node [below]  {} (m-2-2)
	(m-1-3) edge node [below]  {} (m-2-2)
	;
\end{tikzpicture}
\end{enumerate}
For any $\sU \in 	\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right)$ a covering of $\sU$ is a finite family $\left\{\sU_\iota\subset \sU\right\}$ such that $\sU = \bigcup \sU_\iota$. There is an equivalence of sites
\be\label{top_closed_site_eqn}
\left(\mathbf{Hered}/C_0\left(\sX \right), J_{C_0\left(\sX \right)}\right)\cong \left(\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right), J_\sX\right)
\ee
where the Grothendieck topology $J_\sX$ is corresponds to the described above coverings.

\subsection{Sheaves}
\paragraph{}
If $\mathscr F$ is a sheaf on $\sX$ then one can define a presheaf $\mathscr F^c$ on $\left(\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right), J_\sX\right)$ such that
\be\label{top_closed_sheaf_eqn}
\forall \sV \in \mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right)\quad \mathscr F^c\left( \sV\right) \bydef \text{a space of continuous sections of } \mathscr F \text{ over }\sV
\ee
(cf. Remark \ref{sheaf_rem}). 
\begin{lemma}\label{top_sheaf_lem}
The given by \eqref{top_closed_sheaf_eqn} presheaf $\mathscr F^c$ is a sheaf on the site $\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right)$, i.e. $\mathscr F^c\in \mathbf{Sh}\left(\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right) \right)= \mathbf{Sh}\left(\mathfrak{Site}\left( C_0\left(\sX \right) \right) \right)$.

\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
Follows from the Theorem Theorem \ref{loc_fin_french_thm} (cf. English translation  \ref{loc_fin_eng_thm}). !!! CORRECT use \ref{top_soft_flabby_thm}.
\end{proof}
\begin{lemma}\label{top_open_closed_const_lem}
Let $\sX$ be a  compact, locally connected space, and let $F$ be a set. Let $F_\sX$ is a constant presheaf (cf. Definition \ref{constant_presheaf_defn}) and $\mathscr F \bydef \mathfrak{Ass}\left(F_\sX\right)$. If $F_{\left( \mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right) \right)}$ is a a constant presheaf then one has the natural isomorphism
$$
\mathfrak{Ass}\left(F_{\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right)}\right)\cong \mathscr F^c.
$$
where $\mathscr F^c$ is given by \eqref{top_closed_sheaf_eqn}
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
Any $\sU \in \mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right)$ then $\sU$ is compact since it is a closed subset of the compact set $\sX$. It follows that  $\sU$ is a finite disjoint union of compact sets, i.e.
$$
\sU = \bigsqcup_{j = 1}^n \sU_j.
$$
So any $s \in \mathfrak{Ass}\left(F_{\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right)}\right)$ corresponds to a family $\left\lbrace f_1, ..., f_n\right\rbrace \subset F$ where $f_j$ is regarded as an element of $\mathfrak{Ass}\left(F_{\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right)}\right)\left(\sU \right)$ 
Since the space $\sX$ is locally connected there is a family $\left\{\sV_1, ..., \sV_n\right\}$ of connected open subsets of $\sX$ such that
\bean
\forall j = 1,..., n \quad \sU_j\subset \sV_j,\\
j \neq k \quad \sV_j \cap \sV_k = \emptyset
\eean
Any $f_j$ can be regarded as element of $\mathscr F\left( \sV_j\right)$  and the family $\left\lbrace f_1, ..., f_n\right\rbrace$ defines a section $t \in \mathscr F\left(\sV\bydef \bigsqcup_{j=1}^n \sV_j\right)$. On the other hand $t$ is a continuous section of $\mathscr F$ over $\sV$ and $s$ is a restriction of $t$, i.e. $s = t|_{\sU}$. From \ref{top_closed_sheaf_eqn} it follows that $s \in \mathscr F^c\left( \sU\right)$. 
\end{proof}
\begin{definition}\label{top_comm_flasque_defn}
	A sheaf $\mathscr G \in \mathbf{Sh}\left(\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right), J_\sX\right)$ is said to be $\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right)$-\textit{flasque} if for any $\sV \mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right)$ and any $s \in \mathscr G\left(\sV \right)$ there is $t \in  G\left(\sU \right)$ such that $s = t|_\sU$.
\end{definition}
\begin{lemma}\label{top_comm_flasque_lem}
If $\sX$ is a compact Hausdorff space and $\mathscr F \in \mathbf{Sh}\left(\sX \right)$ is a flasque sheaf  (cf. Definition \ref{sheaf_flasque_defn}) then the given by the equation \eqref{top_closed_sheaf_eqn} sheaf $\mathscr F^c \in \mathbf{Sh}\left(\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right), J_\sX\right)$ is $\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right)$-{flasque}.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof} 
If  $\sV\in \mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right)$ then $\sV$ is a closed subset if compact set of $\sX$, so $\sV$ is compact. If $s\in \mathscr F\left(\sV \right)$ then from the Theorem \ref{paracompact_n_thm} it follows that there is an open subset $\sU \subset \sX$ such that  $\sV \subset \sU$ and $t \in s\in \mathscr F\left(\sU \right)$ such that $s = t|_\sV$. On the other hand there is $t' \in \mathscr F\left(\sU \right)$ such that $t = t'|_\sU$ because a sheaf $\mathscr F$ is flasque. It turns out that $s = t'|_\sV$.
\end{proof}
\begin{exercise}\label{sheaf_flasque_c_exer}
	Suppose that $\mathscr A\in \mathbf{Ab}\left(\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right), J_\sX\right)$ is a $\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right)$-flasque sheaf.
\begin{itemize}
	\item[(a)]  If $\mathscr A' \to \mathscr A \to \mathscr A''$ is an exact sequence of $\left(\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right), J_\sX\right)$-sheaves, and if $\mathscr A'$ is $\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right)$-flasque, then for any  $\sU\in \mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right)$ the sequence If $\mathscr A'\left( \sU\right)  \to \mathscr A\left( \sU\right)  \to \mathscr A''\left( \sU\right) $ of Abelian groups is also exact. 
	\item[(b)] If  $\mathscr A' \to \mathscr A \to \mathscr A''$ is an exact sequence of  $\left(\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right), J_\sX\right)$-sheaves, and  if $\mathscr A'$ and $\mathscr A$
are $\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right)$-flasque, then $\mathscr A''$ is $\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right)$ is flasque. 
	%	(d) \i f\X -> Y is a continuous map, and if J^ is a flasque sheaf on X, then /^ 
	%	is a flasque sheaf on X 
	%	(e) Let & be any sheaf on X. We define a new sheafs, called the sheaf of discontinuous sections of J^ as follows. For each open set U c X, ^(U) is the set of 
\end{itemize}
\end{exercise}
\begin{remark}
The exercise \ref{sheaf_flasque_c_exer} is an analog of \ref{sheaf_flasque_exer} one.
\end{remark}
\begin{empt}\label{top_closed_restr_empt}
If  $\mathscr A \in \mathbf{Ab}\left(\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right), J_\sX\right)$ then for any $\sV \in \mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right)$ we define a sheaf  $\mathscr A_\sV \in \mathbf{Ab}\left(\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right), J_\sX\right)$ associated with the presheaf
\be
		\sV' \mapsto \begin{cases}
	\mathscr A\left( \sV'\right) & \sV' \subset \sV\\
	0 & \sV' \not\subset \sV
\end{cases}	.
\ee
This construction is an analog of the Exercise \ref{sheaf_flasque_ext_exer}
\end{empt}
\begin{empt}
If $\Z_{\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right)}$ is a constant sheaf and $\mathscr O\bydef \mathfrak{Ass}\left(\Z_{\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right)} \right) \in  \mathbf{Ab}\left(\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right), J_\sX\right)$ then $\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right)$ becomes a "ringed space". Any  $\mathscr A\in \mathbf{Ab}\left(\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right), J_\sX\right)$ is a sheaf of $\mathscr O$-modules.
\end{empt}
\begin{proposition}\label{sheaf_flasque_closed_ext_prop}
Any $\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right)$ flasque sheaf $\mathcal A \in \mathbf{Ab}\left(\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right), J_\sX\right)$ is acyclic for $\Ga$ (cf. Definition \ref{acyc_defn})
\end{proposition}
\begin{proof}
The proof of this proposition is an analog of the \ref{sheaf_flasque_ext_prop} one.
\end{proof}
	Let $\sX$ be a compact, Hausdorff space, and let $\mathscr F\xrightarrow{f} \mathscr G$ is  $\mathbf{Sh}\left( \sX\right)$-morphism. Let $\mathscr F^c$ and  $\mathscr G^c$ are given by \eqref{top_closed_sheaf_eqn} $\mathbf{Sh}\left(\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right), J_\sX\right)$-objects. If $\sV \in \mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right)$ and $s \in \mathscr F^c\left( \sV\right)$ then from the Theorem \ref{top_soft_flabby_thm} it follows that  there is an open subset $\sU \subset \sX$ and $t \in \mathscr F$ such that $\sV\subset \sU$ and $s = t|_\sV$. One can define $\mathbf{Sh}\left(\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right), J_\sX\right)$-morphism $\mathscr F^c\xrightarrow{f^c} \mathscr G^c$ by the following way
	\be	
	s \mapsto f (t)|_\sV
	\ee 

\begin{lemma}\label{top_image_lem}
In the above situation the image $\im f^c$ (cf. Definition \ref{image_defn}) of $f^c$ is given by 
\bean
\forall \sV \in \mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right)\quad \im f^c\left( \sV\right) \bydef \mathrm{~a~space~of~continuous~sections~of~} \im f \mathrm{ ~over~ }\sV.
\eean
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
From the Remark \ref{sheaf_image_rem} it follows that for any $s \in \im f^c\left( \sV\right)$ there is a finite family $\left\{\sV_1, ..., \sV_n\right\}\subset \mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right)$ and $s_j \in \mathscr F^c\left( \sV_j\right)$ for all $j = 1,..., n$ such that
\bean
\sV_j \cap \sV_k \neq \emptyset\quad \Rightarrow \quad \left. f^c\left(s_j \right)\right|_{\sV_j \cap \sV_k}= \left. f^c\left(s_k \right)\right|_{\sV_j \cap \sV_k}
\eean 
From the Theorem \ref{loc_fin_french_thm} (cf. English translation  \ref{loc_fin_eng_thm}) it follows that the family $\left\{f\left(s_1 \right), ..., f\left(s_1 \right) \right\}$ uniquely defines an element of {the space of continuous sections of } $\mathscr F$ \text{ over }$\sV$.
\end{proof}



\subsection{Sheaf cohomology}
\paragraph{}


\begin{theorem}\label{top_coh_thm}
If $\sX$ is a compact Hausdorff space then for $\mathscr A\in \mathbf{Ab}\left( \sX\right)$ and  any $p$ there is a natural isomorphism
$$
H^p\left(\sX,  \mathscr A\right) \cong H^p\left(\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right),  \mathscr A^c\right)
$$
where $\mathscr A^c\in \mathbf{Ab}\left( \mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right)\right) $ is given by the equation \eqref{top_closed_sheaf_eqn}.
\end{theorem}
\begin{proof}
There is the  given by  \eqref{canonical_resolution_eqn} canonical resolution 	
\be\label{canonical_resolution_c_eqn}
0 \to \mathscr A \xrightarrow{\eps} 	\mathscr{C}^{0}\left(\sX, \mathscr A \right) \xrightarrow{d_0 } \mathscr{C}^{1}\left(\sX, \mathscr A \right)\xrightarrow{d_1 } \mathscr{C}^{2}\left(\sX, \mathscr A \right)\xrightarrow{d_2}\dots
\ee	
Applying the functor $\Ga$ one has a complex
\be\label{top_open_eqn}
\Ga\left(\sX,\ 	\mathscr{C}^{0}\left(\sX, \mathscr A \right)  \right) \xrightarrow{\Ga\left( d_0 \right)} \Ga\left(\sX,	\mathscr{C}^{1}\left(\sX, \mathscr A \right) \right) \xrightarrow{\Ga\left( d_1 \right)} \Ga\left(\sX, 	\mathscr{C}^{2}\left(\sX, \mathscr A \right)  \right) \to ... 
~.\ee
For any $p$ a sheaf $\mathscr{C}^{0}\left(\sX, \mathscr A \right)$ is flasque , so it is acyclic for $\Ga$ (cf. \ref{sheaf_flasque_ext_prop}). From the Theorem \ref{acyc_prop} one has  the $p^{\text{th}}$ cohomology
group 

\bean
\begin{split}
	H^p\left(\sX, \mathscr A \right)=\begin{cases}
		\ker \Ga\left( d_0 \right) & p = 0\\
		\ker~ \Ga\left( d_p \right) / \im~ \Ga\left(  d_{p-1}\right)   & p > 0
	\end{cases}~~.
\end{split}
\eean
If $\mathscr{C}^{p}\left(\sX, \mathscr A \right)^c$ is a  given by \eqref{top_closed_sheaf_eqn} $\mathbf{Sh}\left(\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right), J_\sX\right)$-object then from the Remark \ref{sheaf_image_rem} and the Lemma \ref{top_image_lem} if follows that the sequence 
\bean
0 \to \mathscr A^c \xrightarrow{\eps} 	\mathscr{C}^{0}\left(\sX, \mathscr A \right)^c \xrightarrow{d^c_0 } \mathscr{C}^{1}\left(\sX, \mathscr A \right)^c\xrightarrow{d^c_1 } \mathscr{C}^{2}\left(\sX, \mathscr A \right)^c\xrightarrow{d^c_2}\dots
\eean
is exact (cf. Definition \ref{exact_sec_defn}). From the Lemma \ref{top_comm_flasque_lem}  it follows that for all $p$ the sheaf $\mathscr{C}^{0}\left(\sX, \mathscr A \right)^c$ is  $\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right)$-{flasque}
From the Proposition \ref{sheaf_flasque_closed_ext_prop} it follows that $\mathscr{C}^{0}\left(\sX, \mathscr A \right)^c$ is acyclic for $\Ga$ (cf. Definition \ref{acyc_defn}). If we apply the functor $\Ga\left(\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right), \cdot \right)$ then we obtain a complex
\be\label{top_closed_eqn}
\begin{split}
\Ga\left(\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right),\ 	\mathscr{C}^{0}\left(\sX, \mathscr A \right)^c  \right) \xrightarrow{\Ga\left( d^c_0 \right)} \Ga\left(\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right),	\mathscr{C}^{1}\left(\sX, \mathscr A \right)^c \right) \xrightarrow{\Ga\left( d^c_1 \right)}\\\xrightarrow{\Ga\left( d^c_1 \right)} \Ga\left(\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right), 	\mathscr{C}^{2}\left(\sX, \mathscr A \right)^c  \right) \to ... 
\end{split}
\ee
 From the Proposition \ref{acyc_prop} it follows that
 	\bean
 \begin{split}
 	 H^p\left(\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right),  \mathscr A^c\right)=\begin{cases}
 		\ker \Ga\left( d^c_0 \right) & p = 0\\
 		\ker~ \Ga\left(  d^c_{p} \right) / \im~ \Ga\left(  d^c_{p-1}\right)   & p > 0
 	\end{cases}
 \end{split}
 \eean
However the complex \eqref{top_open_eqn} is naturally isomorphic to \eqref{top_closed_eqn} one, it follows that
\bean
\forall p\ge 0 \quad	H^p\left(\sX, \mathscr A \right)=\begin{cases}
	\ker \Ga\left( d_0 \right) & p = 0\\
	\ker~ \Ga\left( d_p \right) / \im~ \Ga\left(  d_{p-1}\right)   & p > 0
\end{cases}~~=\\
=  	 H^p\left(\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right),  \mathscr A^c\right)=\begin{cases}
	\ker \Ga\left( d^c_0 \right) & p = 0\\
	\ker~ \Ga\left(  d^c_{p} \right) / \im~ \Ga\left(  d^c_{p-1}\right)   & p > 0
\end{cases}.
\eean 
\end{proof}
\subsection{\v{C}ech cohomology}
\begin{lemma}\label{top_open_closed_p_cech_lem}\cite{rae:ctr_morita}
PAGE 104 !!! DOWN !!!  !!! DO NOT DELETE !!!	Lemma 4.77. Suppose $F_1,, . . . , F_n$ are closed subsets of a normal space $\sZ$, and
	$W_{\iota j}$ are open neighborhoods %of F_\iota for 1  i, j  n. Then there are open
	neighborhoods Ni of Fi such that Ni ? Nj ? Wij for all i, j.
\end{lemma}
\begin{lemma}\label{top_open_closed_pp_cech_lem}
Lemma 4.84. Let F1, . . . , Fn be closed subsets of a normal space, and Wijk open
neighborhoods of Fi ? Fj ? Fk for all i, j, k. Then there are open neighbourhoods
Ni of Fi such that Ni ? Nj ? Nk ? Wijk for all i, j, k.
\end{lemma}
\begin{lemma}\label{top_open_closed_cech_lem}
	If $\sX$ is a compact locally connected space then one has:
	\begin{enumerate}
		\item [(i)] for any finite covering $\left\{\sU_\iota \right\}_{\iota = 1,..., m}$ of $\sX$ by open subsets there is a finite  covering $\left\{\sV_\iota \right\}_{\iota = }$ of $\sX$ by closed  subsets such that 
		\be\label{top_open_closed_cech_eqn}
		\begin{split}
			\forall \iota \quad \sV_\iota \subset \sU_\iota,\\
			\forall \left(\iota_0, ..., \iota_{n-1}\right)\in \left\{1,..., m\right\}^n \quad \sU_{\iota_0} \cap ... \cap \sU_{\iota_{n-1}}\neq \emptyset\quad \Leftrightarrow \quad \sV_{\iota_0} \cap ... \cap \sV_{\iota_{n-1}}\neq \emptyset,
		\end{split}
		\ee
		\item[(ii)]  for any finite covering $\left\{\sV_\iota \right\}_{\iota = 1,..., m}$ of $\sX$ by closed subsets there is a finite  covering $\left\{\sU_\iota \right\}_{\iota = 1,..., m}$ of $\sX$ by open  subsets which satisfies to the condition \eqref{top_open_closed_cech_eqn}.
	\end{enumerate}
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
	(i)  For any $\iota  = 1,..., m$ and any $x_\iota \in \sU_\iota$ we select a compact neighborhood $\sV_{x_\iota}$ such that $\sV_{x_\iota}\subset \sU_\iota$. If $\sU_{x_\iota}$ is an open subset of  $\sV_{x_\iota}$ such that ${x_\iota}\subset \sU_{x_\iota}$ then one has $\sX = \bigcup_{x_\iota}\sU_{x_\iota}= \sX$. The set $\sX$ is compact so there is a finite set $\left\{x^1_{1}, ..., x^{k_1}_1,...,x^1_{m}, ..., x^{k_m}_1\right\}$ such that
	\be\label{top_un1_eqn}
	\sX = \bigcup_{\iota = 1}^m \left(\bigcup_{p = 1}^{k_\iota}  \sU_{x^p_\iota}\right).	
	\ee
	The set  $\sV'_\iota \bydef  \bigcup_{p = 1}^{k_\iota}  \sV_{x^p_\iota}$ is closed for any $\iota  = 1,..., m$ and from the equation \eqref{top_un1_eqn} it follows that 	$\bigcup_{\iota = 1}^m \sV'_\iota = \sX$.  For any $n$ and $\left(\iota_0, ..., \iota_{n-1}\right)\in \left\{1,..., m\right\}^n$ such $\sU_{\iota_0} \cap ... \cap \sU_{\iota_{n-1}}\neq \emptyset$ we select a point $x_{\iota_0, ..., \iota_{n-1}}\in \sU_{\iota_0} \cap ... \cap \sU_{\iota_{n-1}}$. If
	$$
	\sV_\iota \bydef \sV'_\iota \cup \left(\bigcup_{\substack{ \iota \in \left\{\iota_0, ..., \iota_{n-1}\right\}}} \left\{x_{\iota_0, ..., \iota_{n-1}}\right\}\right) 
	$$
	then the family $\left\{\sV_\iota \right\}_{\iota \in I}$ satisfies to the condition \ref{top_open_closed_cech_eqn}.\\
	(ii) Since $\sX$ is compact  any $\left(\iota_0, ..., \iota_{n-1}\right)\in \left\{1,..., m\right\}^n \quad \sV_{\iota_0} \cap ... \cap \sV_{\iota_{n-1}}\neq \emptyset$ and any $\iota$ such that $\sV_{\iota_0} \cap ... \cap \sV_{\iota_{n-1}}\cap \sV_\iota = \emptyset$ we select open sets $\sU'_\iota$ and $\sU^\iota_{\iota_0, ..., \iota_{n-1}}$ such that 
	\bean
	\sV_\iota \subset \sU_\iota,\\
	\sV^\iota_{\iota_0, ..., \iota_{n-1}}\subset \sU^\iota_{\iota_0, ..., \iota_{n-1}},\\
	\sU_\iota\cap \sU^\iota_{\iota_0, ..., \iota_{n-1}} = \emptyset.
	\eean
	For any $\left(\iota_0, ..., \iota_{n-1}\right)\in \left\{1,..., m\right\}^n $ such that $\sV_{\iota_0} \cap ... \cap \sV_{\iota_{n-1}}\neq \emptyset$ the finite intersection 
	$$
	\sU_{\iota_0, ..., \iota_{n-1}} \bydef \bigcap_{\iota \notin \left\{\iota_0, ..., \iota_{n-1}\right\}} \sU^\iota_{\iota_0, ..., \iota_{n-1}}
	$$
	is an open set. If 
	\bean
	\sU \bydef \bigcup_{\substack{\left(\iota_0, ..., \iota_{n-1}\right)\in \left\{1,..., m\right\}^n\\\sV_{\iota_0} \cap ... \cap \sV_{\iota_{n-1}}}\neq \emptyset} \sU_{\iota_0, ..., \iota_{n-1}},\\
	\sV'_\iota \bydef \sV_\iota \setminus \sU
	\eean
	then one has
	$$
	\bigcup_{\iota = 1}^m \sV'_\iota = \bigsqcup_{\iota = 1}^m \sV'_\iota
	$$
	Since the space $\sX$ is normal there is a family of open sets $\left\{\sU''_\iota\right\}_{\iota =1,..., m}$ such that
	\bean
	\sV'_\iota\subset \sU''_\iota,\\
	\iota' \neq \iota'' \quad \Rightarrow \quad \sU_{\iota'}\cap \sU_{\iota''}= \emptyset.
	\eean
	If
	$$
	\sU_\iota \bydef \sU''_\iota \cup \left(\bigcup_{\substack{\left(\iota_0, ..., \iota_{n-1}\right)\in \left\{1,..., m\right\}^n\\\iota \in \left\{\iota_0, ..., \iota_{n-1}\right\}}}  \right) \sU_{\iota_0, ..., \iota_{n-1}}
	$$
	then a family $\left\{\sU_\iota \right\}_{\iota \in I}$ of open sets satisfies to the conditions \eqref{top_open_closed_cech_eqn}.
\end{proof}
\begin{remark}
The part (ii) of the Lemma \ref{top_open_closed_cech_lem} is modification of the  \ref{top_open_closed_p_cech_lem} one.
\end{remark}
	
\begin{lemma}\label{top_cech_cof_cov_lem}
Let  $\left\{\sU_\la\right\}_{\la \in \La}$ (resp. $\left\{\sV_\th\right\}_{\th \in \Th}$) be  finite coverings of $\sX$ by open (resp. closed) sets. There are  refinements $\left\{\sU_\iota \right\}_{\iota \in I}$ and $\left\{\sV_\iota \right\}_{\iota \in I}$ of  $\left\{\sU_\la\right\}_{\la \in \La}$ and $\left\{\sV_\th\right\}_{\th \in \Th}$ which satisfy to condition \eqref{top_open_closed_cech_eqn}.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
Let $\left\{\sV_\la\right\}_{\la \in \La}$  be a closed covering of $\sX$ given by (i)  of the Lemma \ref{top_open_closed_cech_lem} i.e
\bean
\begin{split}
	\forall \la \quad \sV_\la \subset \sU_\la,\\
	\forall \left(\la_0, ..., \la_{n-1}\right)\in I^n \quad \sU_{\la_0} \cap ... \cap \sU_{\la_{n-1}}\neq \emptyset\quad \Leftrightarrow \quad \sV_{\la_0} \cap ... \cap \sV_{\la_{n-1}}\neq \emptyset.
\end{split}\eean 
If $\left\{\sV_\iota \right\}_{\iota \in I}$ is a refinement of both $\left\{\sV_\la\right\}_{\la \in \La}$ and $\left\{\sV_\th\right\}_{\th \in \Th}$ then there is a map $\phi : I \to \La$ such that $\sV_\iota \subset \sV_{\phi\left(\iota \right) }$. Otherwise from (ii) of the Lemma   \ref{top_open_closed_cech_lem}   one has a family $\left\{\sU'_\iota \right\}_{\iota \in I}$ such that
\bean
\begin{split}
	\forall \iota \quad \sV_\iota \subset \sU'_\iota,\\
	\forall \left(\iota_0, ..., \iota_{n-1}\right)\in I^n \quad \sU'_{\iota_0} \cap ... \cap \sU'_{\iota_{n-1}}\neq \emptyset\quad \Leftrightarrow \quad \sV_{\iota_o} \cap ... \cap \sV_{\iota_{n-1}}\neq \emptyset,
\end{split}
\eean
If we define $\sU_\iota \bydef \sU'_\iota \cap \sU_{\phi\left( \iota\right)}$  then for all $\iota \in I$ one has $\sU_\iota \subset \sU_{\phi\left(\iota \right) }$ i.e. $\left\{\sU_\iota\right\}_{\iota \in I}$ is a refinement of $\left\{\sU_\la\right\}_{\la \in \La}$. Moreover one has

\be\label{top_open_closed_t_cech_eqn}
\begin{split}
	\forall \iota \quad \sV_\iota \subset \sU_\iota,\\
	\forall \left(\iota_0, ..., \iota_{n-1}\right)\in I^n \quad \sU_{\iota_0} \cap ... \cap \sU_{\iota_{n-1}}\neq \emptyset\quad \Leftrightarrow \quad \sV_{\iota_0} \cap ... \cap \sV_{\iota_{n-1}}\neq \emptyset,
\end{split}
\ee
so this  lemma is proven.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}\label{cech_n_thm}
If $\sX$ is a compact  space then for $\mathscr A\in \mathbf{Ab}\left( \sX\right)$ and  any $p$ there is a natural isomorphism
\be\label{cech_n_eqn}
\check H^p\left(\sX,  \mathscr A\right) \cong \check H^p\left(\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right),  \mathscr A^c\right)
\ee
where $\mathscr A^c\in \mathbf{Ab}\left( \mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right)\right) $ is given by the equation \eqref{top_closed_sheaf_eqn}.
\end{theorem}
\begin{proof}
According to the Remark \ref{top_chech_cof_rem} one can use only finite open coverings of $\sX$ for calculation of $\check H^p\left(\sX,  \mathscr A\right)$.
According to \eqref{top_open_closed_t_cech_eqn} for any $p$ one has isomorphism
\be\label{cech_n_iso_eqn}
\check H^p\left(\left\{\sU_\iota \right\}_{\iota \in I},  \mathscr A\right) \cong \check H^p\left(\left\{\sV_\iota \right\}_{\iota \in I},  \mathscr A^c\right).
\ee
On the other hand the given by the Lemma \ref{top_cech_cof_cov_lem} systems of coverings  $\left\{\sU_\iota \right\}_{\iota \in I}$ and $\left\{\sV_\iota \right\}_{\iota \in I}$ are cofinal in the sites $\sX$ and $\left(\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right), J_\sX\right)$ respectively, so from  \eqref{cech_n_iso_eqn} one can obtain isomorphisms \eqref{cech_n_eqn}.

\end{proof}

\begin{remark}
	The commutative  Gelfand-Na\u{\i}mark theorem \ref{gelfand-naimark_thm} states the duality between commutative $C^*$-algebra and its spectrum. The Lemma \ref{top_sheaf_lem} and the Theorems  \ref{top_coh_thm}
\ref{cech_n_thm} are motivations of the "Gelfand $A$-site" and  "Gelfand $A$-topos" terms (cf. Definition \ref{gelfand_a_site_defn}).
\end{remark}


\section{Topoi of continuous trace  $C^*$-algebras}

\paragraph{}
Let $CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)$ the stable
continuous-trace algebra  with DixmierDouady class $\delta \in \check{H}^3\left(\sX,\Z \right)$ (cf. Notation \ref{ctr_not}). Suppose that the space $\sX$ is compact. If $B \subset  CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)$ is a hereditary subalgebra then from  \ref{ctr_rep_eq_lem} it follows that for any $a \in CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)$ a subset 
$$
\sX_a \bydef \left\{x \in \sX | \left\| \mathfrak{rep}_x\left(a \right) \right\| > 0\right\}\subset \sX
$$
is open (where $\mathfrak{rep}_x$ is given by \eqref{rep_x_eqn})
\begin{definition}\label{ctr_supp_defn}
	If $B$ is a hereditary $C^*$-subalgebra  of $A$ then a given by
	\be\label{ctr_supp_eqn}
	\cosupp B \bydef \sX \setminus \bigcup_{a \in B} \sX_a
	\ee
	closed subset of $\sX$ is said to be a \textit{cosupport} of $B$.
\end{definition}
Consider a presheaf $C^\sX$ on the category $\mathfrak{Closed}\left(\sX\right)$ (cf. Section \ref{top_closed_sec}) such that for any $\mathfrak{Closed}\left(\sX\right)$-object $\sU$ one has
\be\label{top_cx_eqn}
C^\sX\left(\sU  \right) \bydef CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)|^\sU
\ee
where the notation \ref{closed_ideal_eqn} is used.
\begin{lemma}\label{ctr_sh_lem}
The given by \eqref{top_cx_eqn} presheaf is a $\left(\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right), J_\sX\right)$ sheaf  (cf. \eqref{top_closed_site_eqn}).
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
!!!	
\end{proof}
From the Theorem \ref{dauns_hofmann_thm} it follows that there is the natural inclusion $\varphi: C\left( \sX \right) \subset M\left( CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)\right)$ which satisfies to the Definition \ref{hereditary_full_defn}, so the Lemma \ref{geometric_morphism_thm} yields  a  morphism of sites 
\bean
\mathfrak{Site}\left( CT\left(\sX, \dl \right) \right) \xrightarrow{\mathfrak{Site}(\varphi)}\mathfrak{Site}\left( C\left( \sX \right)\right) 
\eean
(cf. Definition \ref{morphism_of_sites_defn}) and a natural geometric morphism
\bean
\mathfrak{Topos}\left( CT\left(\sX, \dl \right) \right) \xrightarrow{\mathfrak{Topos}(\varphi)}\mathfrak{Topos}\left(C\left( \sX \right)\right) 
\eean
(cf. Definition \ref{geometric_morphism_defn}). From the equation \eqref{top_closed_site_eqn} it turns out that the above morphism of sites and geometric morphism are equivalent to following morphisms 
\bea\label{ctr_site_morphism_eqn} 
\mathfrak{Site}\left( CT\left(\sX, \dl \right) \right) \xrightarrow{\mathfrak{Site}(\varphi)}\left(\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right), J_\sX\right),\\ 
\label{ctr_geometric_morphism_eqn} 
\mathfrak{Topos}\left( CT\left(\sX, \dl \right) \right) \xrightarrow{\mathfrak{Topos}(\varphi)}\mathbf{Sh}\left(\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right), J_\sX\right). 
\eea
If $U' \bydef UM\left( CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)\right)$ and  $A' \bydef\Aut_{C\left(\sX\right)}\left( CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)\right)$ then for any $\sU \in \mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right)$ there are equivalence relations
\bean
\forall u', u'' \in U' \quad u' \sim_\sU u'' \quad \Leftrightarrow \quad \forall x \in ( CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)\quad \left(u'- u'' \right)x \in CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)|_{\sX \setminus\sU},\\
\forall a', a'' \in A' \quad a' \sim_\sU a'' \quad \Leftrightarrow \quad \forall x \in ( CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)\quad \left(a'- a'' \right)x \in CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)|_{\sX \setminus\sU}
\eean
where  $CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)|_{\sX \setminus\sU}$ is given by \eqref{open_ideal_eqn}. One can define presheaves $U^\sX, \A^\sX \in \mathbf{PreSh}\left(\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right), J_\sX\right)$ of groups such that for any $\mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right)$-object $\sU$ one has
\bean
U^\sX \left(\sU  \right)\bydef U' /\sim_\sU,\\ 
A^\sX \left(\sU  \right)\bydef A' /\sim_\sU,\\ 
\eean
Similarly to the Lemma \ref{ctr_sh_lem} one can proof that both $U^\sX$ and $A^\sX$ are sheaves.  If $S^\sX$ is a sheaf of germs of continuous maps $\sX \to \T$ then one has
$$
A^\sX = U^\sX / S^\sX
$$
(cf. !!!).
Denote by
\bean
U^A \bydef \mathfrak{Topos}(\varphi)^* U^\sX,\\

\eean
where $\mathfrak{Topos}(\varphi)^*$ is the inverse image (cf. Definition \ref{geometric_morphism_defn}) of the given by \eqref{ctr_geometric_morphism_eqn} geometric morphism. 
If   $\dl^2 \in \check H^2\left(\mathbf{Sh}\left(\mathfrak{Closed}\left(\sX\right)\right)  , S \right)$
is the preimage of $\dl \in H^3\left(\mathbf{Sh}\left(\mathfrak{Closed}\left(\sX\right)\right)  , \Z \right)$
then there is a finite set $\mathscr U = \left\lbrace \sU_1, ..., \sU_n \right\rbrace $ such that $\dl^2$ is represented by $c^S_\sX = \left[\nu_{\iota, j, k}\right]\in \Z^2\left( \mathscr U, \T\right)$. On the other hand $c^S_\sX = \Dl c^A_\sX$ where $c^A_\sX= \left[ \a_{\iota j}  \right) \in \Z^1\left( \mathscr U, A\right)$ and  $\Dl$ is an explained in \ref{ctr_cycle_map_empt} map. If $\mathscr U$ is such that $\a_{\iota j} = \mathrm{Ad}u_{\iota j}$ where $\a_{\iota j}\in A\left( \sU_\iota \cap \sU_j\right)$ and $u_{\iota j}\in U\left( \sU_\iota \cap \sU_j\right)$ then according to \eqref{ctr_vijk_eqn} one has
	\be\label{ctr_vijk_p_eqn}
\forall z \in \sU_{\iota j k} \quad \nu_{\iota jk}(z)  \quad   \mu_{\iota j}(z)\mu_{j k}(z)\mu^{-1}_{\iota k}
\ee
If we consider a map \eqref{ctr_site_morphism_eqn} then 
$$
\mathfrak{Site}(\varphi)^{-1}\left(\sU_\iota \right) =  CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)|_{\sX \setminus \sU_\iota}
$$
where the ideal $CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)|_{\sX \setminus \sU_\iota}$ is given by the equation \eqref{open_ideal_eqn}.
A family $$
\mathscr U^A\bydef \left\{CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)_{\sX \setminus \sU_1}, ..., CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)_{\sX \setminus \sU_n}\right\}
$$ is a covering of $\{0\} \in \mathbf{Hered}/CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)$, i.e.
$$
CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)|_{\sX \setminus \sU_1}\cap ...\cap CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)_{\sX \setminus \sU_n} = \{0\}
$$
 (cf. Definition \ref{pullback_covering_ca_defn}).
The cycle $c^A_\sX= \left[ \a_{\iota j}  \right] \in Z^1\left( \mathscr U, A\right)$ naturally defines a cycle $c^A_A= \left[ \a^A_{\iota j}  \right] \in \Z^1\left( \mathscr U^A, A^A\right)$. However the cycle $\left[ \a^A_{\iota j}  \right]$ yields global section $1_{CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)}\in A^A\left(\{0\} \right) $ of $A^A$, so one has $\left[ \a^A_{\iota j}  \right]\in D^0\left(  \mathscr U^A, A^A\right)$ (cf. \eqref{nonab_perm_eqn}, \eqref{nonab_coh_q_eqn}), i.e. $c^A_A$ is a trivial cycle in $H^1\left(\mathfrak{Site}\left(CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)\right) , A^A \right)$.



Similarly to \ref{ctr_cycle_map_empt}  and the Lemma \ref{ctr_cycle_map_lem} one can construct an isomorphism
\be\label{ctr_p12_eqn}
\check H^1\left( \mathfrak{Site}\left(CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)\right) A^A\right)\xrightarrow[\cong]{\phi_{1,2} } \check H^2\left(\mathfrak{Site}\left(CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)\right), S^A \right). 
\ee
and $\phi_{1,2} \left( \left[ \a^A_{\iota j}  \right]\right)= 0$ since $\left[ \a^A_{\iota j}  \right]$ is trivial in $H^1\left(\mathfrak{Site}\left(CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)\right) , A^A \right)$.
From the Lemma \ref{cech_geom_lem} it follows that there are natural homomorphisms
\bea\label{ctr_h2_eqn}
\check H^2\left(\mathbf{Sh}\left(\mathfrak{Closed}\left(\sX\right)\right)  , S \right) \xrightarrow{\check{H}^2\left(\T \right) } \check H^2\left(\mathbf{Sh}\left( \mathfrak{Site}\left( CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)\right)\right) , S^A \right),\\
\check H^3\left(\mathbf{Sh}\left(\mathfrak{Closed}\left(\sX\right)\right)  , \Z \right) \xrightarrow{\check{H}^3\left(\Z \right) } \check H^3\left(\mathbf{Sh}\left( \mathfrak{Site}\left( CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)\right)\right) , \Z \right)
\eea
and taking into account  $\phi_{1,2} \left( \left[ \a^A_{\iota j}  \right]\right)= 0$ one has $\check{H}^2\left(\T \right)\left(\dl^2 \right) = 0$.
 \begin{theorem}\label{ctr_main_thm}
	Suppose that  $CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)=\Ga\left(E \right) $ is a  set of sections a locally
	trivial bundle with fibre $\K(\H)$ and structure group $\Aut~ \K(\H)$ over the   space $\sX$ with transition functions $\a_{\iota, j}$. If  $\dl^2 \bydef \Dl\left(\left[\a_{\iota j}\right] \right) \in H^2\left( \sX, S\right) \cong H^3\left( \sX,\Z \right)$  represents $\dl \in H^3\left( \sX,\Z \right)$ (cf. Proposition \ref{ctr_dd_prop}), and $\check{H}^2\left(\T \right)$ is given by \eqref{ctr_h2_eqn} then
\bea\label{ctr_h20_ker_eqn}
\ker \check{H}^2\left(\T \right) = 	\Z \dl^2,\\
\label{ctr_h30_ker_eqn}
\ker \check{H}^3\left(\Z \right) = 	\Z \dl.
\eea
\end{theorem}
\begin{proof}
From the isomorphism \eqref{ctr_p12_eqn} it follows that a cocycle $c \in Z^2\left(\mathfrak{Site}\left(CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)\right), S^A \right)$ satisfies to  $\left[c\right]= 0 \in Z^2\left(\mathfrak{Site}\left(CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)\right), S^A \right)$ if it equals to $\Dl\left(\left\{\a'_{\iota j}\right\} \right)$ such that  $\left[\a'_{\iota j}\right]$ is a trivial element of $\check H^1\left( \mathfrak{Site}\left(CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)\right) A^A\right)$, i.e. $\left[\a'_{\iota j}\right]\in D\left( \mathfrak{Site}\left(CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)\right), S^A\right)$ (cf. \eqref{nonab_perm_eqn})

\end{proof}

 \begin{lem}\label{ctr_main_lem}
	Suppose that  $CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)=\Ga\left(E \right) $ is a  set of sections a locally
	trivial bundle with fibre $\K(\H)$ and structure group $\Aut~ \K(\H)$ over the   space $\sX$ with transition functions $\a_{\iota j}$. If  $\Dl\left(\left[\a_{\iota j}\right] \right) \in H^2\left( \sX, S\right) \cong H^3\left( \sX,\Z \right)$  represents $\dl \in H^3\left( \sX,\Z \right)$ (cf. Proposition \ref{ctr_dd_prop}) then 
	\bea\label{ctr_h20_eqn}
	\check{H}^2\left(\T \right)\left( \Dl\left(\left[\a_{\iota j}\right] \right)\right) = 0,\\\label{ctr_h30_eqn}
	\check{H}^3\left(\Z \right)\left(\dl \right)  = 0.
	\eea
	where $\check{H}^2\left(\T \right)$ and $\check{H}^3\left(\Z \right)$ are given by the equations \eqref{ctr_h2_eqn} and \eqref{ctr_h3_eqn} respectively.
\end{lem}
\begin{proof}
	The equation \eqref{ctr_h20_eqn} is already proven.

\end{proof}

So one can deduce that is $B$ is a hereditary $C^*$-subalgebra and $S'(B)$ is a group of continuous maps from $\cosupp B \to \T$ then there is a natural injective homomorphism of groups $S'\left(B\right) \to U^A\left( B\right)$. One has a presheaf $B \mapsto S'\left( B\right)$. If
\be\label{ctr_sa_eqn}
S^A \bydef \mathfrak{Ass}\left( B \mapsto S'\left(B\right)\right) 
\ee 
where $\mathfrak{Ass}$ means an associated sheaf (cf. Definition \ref{associated_sheaf_defn}).
From the *-homomorphism $\varphi : C\left( \sX \right) \hookto M\left( CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)\right)$ and the  On the other hand from  \eqref{top_closed_site_eqn} it follows that there is a natural isomorphism of sites $\mathfrak{Site}\left( C\left( \sX \right)\right)\cong \mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right)$. If $S \in \mathbf{Ab}\left( \mathfrak{Closed}\left( \sX\right)\right)$ is a sheaf of germs of continuous maps from $\sX$ to $\T$ then one can proof that
\be\label{ctr_t_ii_eqn}
S^A = \mathfrak{Topos}(\varphi)^* (S)
\ee
where $\mathfrak{Topos}(\varphi)^*$ is the inverse image of $\mathfrak{Topos}(\varphi)$ (cf. Definition \ref{geometric_morphism_defn}) $S^A  \in \mathbf{Ab}\left( \mathfrak{Site}\left( CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)\right)\right)$ is given by the equation \eqref{ctr_sa_eqn}.

From \eqref{const_sheaf_morphism_eqn} and the Lemma \ref{cech_geom_lem} it follows that there is a homomorphism
\be\label{ctr_h3_eqn}
\check H^3\left(\mathbf{Sh}\left(\mathfrak{Closed}\left(\sX\right)\right)  , \Z \right) \xrightarrow{\check{H}^3\left(\Z \right) } \check H^3\left(\mathbf{Sh}\left( \mathfrak{Site}\left( CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)\right)\right) , \Z \right)
\ee
where the notation \eqref{chech_hom_eqn} is used.

Let $CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)$ the stable
continuous-trace algebra  with DixmierDouady class $\delta \in \check{H}^3\left(\sX,\Z \right)$ (cf. Notation \ref{ctr_not}). Suppose that the space $\sX$ is compact. 	For any hereditary $C^*$-subalgebra of $CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)$ there is a given by the equation \ref{left_ideal_eqn} left ideal $L\left(B\right)$.
From the Theorem \ref{left_ideal_thm} it follows that  	
there is 	 an increasing net $\left\{u_\la\right\}_{\la\in\La}$ of positive elements in the closed unit ball of
$L\left(B\right)$ such that
\be\label{ctr_ul_eqn}
\forall a \in L\left(B\right) \quad a = \lim_{\la\in \La}au_\la. 
\ee
 Let  $\pi: CT\left(\sX, \dl \right) \to B\left( \H\right)$ be the atomic representation  (cf. Definition \ref{atomic_repr_defn}). From the Lemma \ref{increasing_convergent_w_lem} it follows that there is  the limit $p'_B \bydef s$-$\lim_{\la\in \La} \pi\left(  u_\la\right) \in B\left(\H \right)$ with respect to the strong topology (cf. Definition \ref{strong_topology_defn}) of $B\left(\H\right)$. From  $L\left(B\right)M\left(CT\left(\sX, \dl \right) \right)= L\left(B\right)$ and \eqref{ctr_ul_eqn} it follows that $  \forall a \in  M\left(CT\left(\sX, \dl \right) \right)\quad a p'_B = p'_B a$, so one has
 \be\label{ctr_pb_c_eqn}
 p_B \bydef 1_{B\left(\H\right)}-p'_B\quad \Rightarrow \quad \forall a \in  M\left(CT\left(\sX, \dl \right) \right)\quad a p_B = p_B a
 \ee
 Denote by
\be\label{ctr_sh_of_alg}
A^A\left( B\right)  \bydef p_B CT\left(\sX, \dl \right) p_B \subset B\left( \H\right). 
\ee
It is clear that $A^A\left(B \right)$ is a $C^*$-algebra and there is a surjective *-homomorphism $A^A_B:CT\left(\sX, \dl \right) \to A^A\left( B\right)$.  Given $B', B'' \in  \mathbf{Hered}/CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)$ such that $B' \subset B''$ (i.e. there is $\mathbf{Hered}/CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)$-morphism $B'' \to B'$) there is   the natural surjective  *-homomorphism
\be\label{ctr_psh_of_alg}
C^A_{B'B''}:C^A\left( B'\right) \to C^A\left( B''\right).
\ee 
It turns out that a map
\be\label{ctr_psh_defn}
B \mapsto C^A\left( B\right) 
\ee
is a $\mathbf{Hered}/CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)$-presheaf of $C^*$-algebras (cf. Definitions \ref{presheaf_defn} and \ref{hered_cat_defn}).

\begin{lemma}\label{ctr_psh_sh_defn}
A given by \eqref{ctr_psh_defn} presheaf is a sheaf with respect to Gelfand $CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)$-topology (cf. Definition \ref{gelfand-naimark_thm}).
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
If $B$ is a   $\mathbf{Hered}/CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)$-object then a covering of $B$ is a finite family $\left\{B_1, ..., B_n\right\}$ of  $\mathbf{Hered}/CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)$-objects such that  $B = \bigcap_{\iota=1}^n B_\iota$. It follows that $p_B$ is the maximal among the projectors $p \in B\left( \H\right)$ such  that $p < p_{B_\iota}$ for all $\iota = 1,..., n$.
\begin{enumerate}
	\item [(i)] the presheaf is separated (cf. Definition \ref{sheaf_defn}), i.e. the given by \eqref{sheaf_eqn} morphism $\eps$ is a monomorphism,
	\item [(ii)] the  morphism $\eps$ is an epimorphism.
\end{enumerate}
(i) Any $a \in C^A\left( B\right)$ is given by $p_B \widetilde a p_B$  where $\widetilde a \in CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)$. However if  $p_{B_\iota}\widetilde a p_{B_\iota}= 0$ for every $\iota = 1,..., n$ then $p_B \widetilde a p_B = 0$.\\
(ii)  Let  $P \subset  \left\{1, ..., n\right\}^2$ be such that for any $\left(\iota, j\right)\in P$ the generated by a union $B_\iota \cup B_j$ hereditary $C^*$-algebra $B_{\iota j}$ is not $\mathbf{Hered}/CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)$. It follows that $\im p_{B_\iota}\cap \im p_{B_j}\neq \{0\}$ for any $a \in A\left( B\right)$ then there is $\widetilde a \in CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)$ such that $a = p_B \widetilde a p_B$. If $a_\iota \bydef C^A_{BB_\iota} \left(a \right)$ then $a_\iota =  p_{B_\iota} \widetilde a   p_{B_{\iota}}$. 
One should prove that $C^A_{B_\iota B_{\iota j}}\left( a_\iota \right) = C^A_{B_jB_{\iota j}}\left( a_j \right)$. This fact follows from the following equation
\bean
 C^A_{B_\iota B_{\iota j}}\left( a_\iota \right)= C^A_{B_\iota B_{\iota j}}\left( a_j \right)= p_{B_\iota j} \widetilde a   p_{B_{\iota j}}
\eean 
\end{proof}
From \eqref{ctr_pb_c_eqn} it follows that $p_B u = u p_B$ for all $u\in U$, so $U$ there is a natural action $U \times C^A\left(B\right)\to C^A\left( B\right)$. If $U_B$ is a kernel of this action then $U_B$ is a normal subgroup.  
\begin{exercise}
Prove that the map
\be\label{ctr_u_sh_eqn}
U^A : B \mapsto U^A\left(B\right) \bydef U / U_B
\ee
is a sheaf of groups, i.e. $U_A \in \mathbf{Sh}\left(\mathfrak{Site}\left(CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)\right)\right)$ (cf. \eqref{sheaf_notation_eqn}).
\end{exercise}
\begin{remark}
	For any closed subset $F \subset \sX$ there is a hereditary $C^*$-subalgebra
	\be\label{ctr_cosupp_eqn}
	CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)\left(F  \right) \bydef  \text{ the } C^*\text{-norm completion of }  C_0\left(\sX \setminus F \right)CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)C_0\left(\sX \setminus F \right), 
	\ee
	such that $\cosupp  CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)\left(F  \right) = F$. If $\left\{\F_\iota\right\}$ is a family of closed  sets such that $\bigcup F_\iota = \sX$ then $\bigcap CT\left(\sX, \dl \right)\left(F_\iota  \right)= 0$.
\end{remark}

\begin{theorem}
Theorem 4.37. PAGE 85. Suppose that $\sS$ and $\mathcal R$ are, respectively, the sheaves of germs
of continuous $\T$- and $\R$-valued functions on a paracompact space $\sX$. Then for
all $n \ge1$, the connecting homomorphism $\Dl^n$ is an isomorphism of $H^n\left( \sX, \sS\right)$ 
onto $H^{n+1}(\sX,\Z)$. The connecting homomorphism $\Dl^0$ induces an isomorphism
of $ C(\sX,\T)/e(C(\sX,\R))$ onto $H^1\left( \sX, \Z\right)$ . (Here, $e$ denotes the exponential map of
Example 4.12.)
\end{theorem}

\begin{empt}\label{ctr_cycle_map_empt}\cite{rae:ctr_morita}
	PAGE 106 !!!
	We now turn to the Dixmier-Douady classification of bundles with fibre $\K\left( \H\right)$ 
	and structure group $\Aut~ \K(\H)$ over a paracompact space $\sZ$. From Remark 4.54,
	such a bundle is determined up to isomorphism by the class $\left[\a_{\iota j}\right]$ of its transition
	functions in the cohomology set $H^1\left( \sZ, A\right)$ , where $A$ is the sheaf of germs of continuous $\Aut ~\K\left(\H\right)$-valued functions. Proposition 1.6 says that the conjugation map
	$\Ad$ of $U(\H)$ onto $\Aut\K(\H)$ induces a short exact sequence
	\be\label{ctr_exact_eqn}
	1 \to S \to U \xrightarrow{\text{Ad}} A\quad (4.26)
	\ee
	of sheaves, relating the sheaf $A$ to the sheaves $S$ and $U$ of $\T$- and $U(\H)$-valued functions. If these were all sheaves of Abelian groups, this would induce a long exact
	sequence of sheaf cohomology, giving a connecting homomorphism $\Delta  : H^1(\sZ,\A)\to  H^2(\sZ, S)$, which should be injective because $H^1\left( \sZ, U\right)$  is trivial (Proposition 4.76).
	Indeed, because $U$  is soft, one could further anticipate that $H^2(\sZ, \sU)$ might vanish (Remark 4.75), in which case $\Dl$ should be surjective. This reasoning is purely
	speculative: we have not even defined $H^2(\sZ, U)$, and Theorem 4.30 applies only
	to sheaves of Abelian groups. However, because $\T$ is central in $U(\H)$, there is just
	enough commutativity around to make the arguments in Section 4.1 work: we can
	directly construct a map $\Dl$ of $H^1(\sZ,A)$ into $H^2(\sZ, S)$, and prove that it is a bijection. We can then apply the isomorphism $H^2(\sZ, \S) \cong H^3(\sZ;\Z)$ of Theorem 4.42 to
	$\Dl\left(\left[\a_{\iota j}\right] \right)$  to get a class in the topological cohomology group  $H^3(\sZ;\Z)$ which classifies
	the original bundle up to isomorphism.
	We now make all this precise. We shall not assume until we have to that the
	Hilbert space $\H$ is infinite-dimensional.
	To construct $\Dl : H^1(\sZ,A) \to H^2(\sZ, S)$, we follow the procedure of Lemma 4.31.
	Given a cover $\mathscr U$ of $\sZ$, and $\left\{\la_{\iota, j}\right\}\in Z^1(\mathscr U,A)$, we can apply Lemma 4.33 to the
	short exact sequence (4.26); this allows us to assume by passing to a refinement of $\mathscr U$ that there are continuous maps $\mu_{\iota j}: U_{\iota j} \to  U(\H)$ with $\la_{\iota j}(z) = \text{Ad} \mu_{\iota j}(z)$ for
	$z \in \sU_{\iota j}$. Since $\left\{\la_{\iota j}\right\}$ is a cocycle, we have
	$$
	\forall z \in \sU_{\iota j k}\quad  \text{Ad}\left(  \mu_{\iota j}(z)\mu_{j k}(z)\right) = \text{Ad}\left(  \mu_{\iota k}(z)\right)
	$$
	and since $\ker \text{Ad} = \T$ (Lemma 1.5), there are continuous functions $\nu_{\iota jk} : \sU_{\iota jk} \to \T$
	satisfying
	\be\label{ctr_vijk_eqn}
	\forall z \in \sU_{\iota j k}\quad   \mu_{\iota j}(z)\mu_{j k}(z) = \nu_{\iota jk}(z)  \mu_{\iota k}(z)(4.27)
	\ee
	It is a simple matter to check that $\left[\nu_{\iota jk}\right]$ is a 2-cocycle in $Z^2\left(\mathscr U, S \right)$ :
	\be
	\nu_{\iota jk}\nu_{\iota kl} = \mu_{\iota j}\mu_{jk}\mu^{-1}_{\iota k}\mu_{\iota k}\mu_{kl}\mu_{\iota l}^{-1}= \mu_{\iota j}\mu_{jk}\mu_{kl}\mu_{\iota l}^{-1},
	\ee
	whereas
	\be
	\nu_{\iota jk}\nu_{\iota kl} = \mu_{\iota j}\mu_{jl}\mu_{\iota l}^{-1}\nu_{jkl} = \mu_{\iota j}\nu_{jkl}\mu_{jl}\mu_{\iota l}^{-1}
	= \mu_{\iota j}\mu_{jk}\mu_{kl}\mu_{jl}^{-1}\mu_{jl}\mu_{\iota l}^{-1}
	\ee
	!!!
	\be
	\la_{\iota j} = \Id_{C\left(B_{\iota j} \right) }
	\ee
	!!!
\end{empt}
\begin{lemma}\label{ctr_cycle_map_lem}\cite{rae:ctr_morita}
	PAGE 107 !!! Lemma 4.81. Let $\H$ be a Hilbert space, $\sZ$ a paracompact space, and $\left\{\la_{\iota j} \right\} \in Z^1(\mathscr U,A)$ a cocycle with coefficients in the sheaf $A$ of germs of continuous
	$\Aut~\K(\H)$-valued functions on $\sZ$. Then the above procedure gives a class
	$\Dl\left( \left[\la_{\iota j}\right]\right) \bydef \left[\nu_{\iota j k}\right]$ in $H^2(\sZ, S)$ which depends only on the class of $\left\{\la_{\iota j} \right\}$ in
	$H^1(\sZ,A)$, and which vanishes if and only if, possibly after refining the cover, there
	is a cocycle $\left\{\la_{\iota j} \right\}\in Z^1(\mathscr U,U)$ satisfying  $\la_{\iota j}= \mathrm{Ad} \circ \mu_{\iota j} $ for all $\iota$, $j$.
\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
We first note that the class $\left[\nu_{\iota j k}\right]$ does not depend on the choice of liftings
	$\mu_{\iota j}$: Lemma 1.5 implies that any other liftings could, apart from the possible need to
	refine the cover, only differ from $\mu_{\iota j}$ by scalar functions $\rho_{\iota j}: \sU_{\iota j} \to \T$, and then the
	corresponding 2-cocycle would be $\left( d\rho^{-1}\right)\nu$ . If we replace $\left\{ \la_{\iota j} \right\}$ by the equivalent
	cocycle $\left\{\eta_\iota \la_{\iota j} \eta_\iota^{-1}\right\}$, we can by refining the cover $\left\{\sU_\iota\right\}$ assume that $\eta_\iota = \mathrm{Ad}\zeta_\iota$ for
	some continuous maps $\zeta_\iota : \sU_\iota \to U\left(\H \right)$ , and then $\mathrm{Ad} \circ\left(\zeta_\iota \mu_{\iota j} \zeta_\iota^{-1}\right)=\eta_\iota \la_{\iota j} \eta_\iota^{-1}$. With
	this choice of liftings, we obtain exactly the same cocycle $\left\{\nu_{\iota jk}\right\}$. So we have a well-
	defined map $\Dl$ of $H^1(Z,A)$ into $H^2(Z, S)$, which clearly vanishes on the image of
	$H^1(Z, U)$  that is, if we could have found $\mu_{\iota j}$ which formed a cocycle. Conversely,
	if $\Dl\left(\left[\la_{\iota j}\right]\right)=0$, then again after refining the cover, $\nu_{\iota jk}$ has the form $d\left( \rho_{\iota j}\right)$  for some $\rho_{\iota j}\in C^1\left( \mathscr U, S\right)$, and then $\left\{\rho^{-1}_{\iota j}\mu_{\iota j}\right\}$ is a cocycle with $\mathrm{Ad}\circ \left(\rho^{-1}_{\iota j}\mu_{\iota j} \right) = \la_{\iota j}$
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}\label{ctr_dd_prop}
	Proposition 5.36. PAGE 135 !!! Suppose $\H$ is a Hilbert space, and $p: E\to T$ is a locally
	trivial bundle with fibre $\K(\H)$ and structure group $\Aut~ \K(\H)$ over a paracompact
	locally compact space $T$, with transition functions $\a_{\iota, j}$. Then
	$\Ga_0\left( E\right)$ is a continuous-trace $C^*$-algebra with spectrum $T$ and Dixmier-Douady class
	$\Dl\left(\left[\a_{\iota j}\right] \right) \in H^2\left( T, S\right) \cong H^3\left( \sX,\Z \right)$. 
\end{proposition}
\begin{lemma}
PAGE 141. !!! Lemma 5.47. Suppose $A$ is a continuous-trace $C^*$-algebra with spectrum $T$, $\a \in \Aut_{C_0\left( T\right) }~ A$, and $t \in T$. Then there are a compact neighborhood $F$ of $T$ and a
unitary multiplier $u \in UM\left(A|^F \right)$  such that $\a^F = \mathrm{Ad}u$.
\end{lemma}
\begin{theorem}
	PAGE 140
	Theorem 5.42. Suppose that $A$ is a continuous-trace $C^*$-algebra with spectrum $T$.
	Then there is a homomorphism $\zeta :\Aut_{C_0\left( T \right)}A\to H^2\left( T, \Z\right)$  such that
	$$
	0 \to \mathrm{Inn}~ A \to \Aut_{C_0\left( T \right)} A\xrightarrow{\zeta} H^2\left( T, \Z\right)
	$$
	
	is an exact sequence of groups. If $A$ is stable, then $\zeta$ is surjective.
\end{theorem}
\begin{proof}

Example 4.25. If $n = 0$ (and $\sS$ is a sheaf), then $H^0\left(\mathscr U, \sS \right)$ coincides with
$Z^0\left(\mathscr U, \sS \right)$. Since $f = \left\{f_\iota\right\}$ satisfies $d\left( f\right)= 0$  if and only if there exists F ? S(X)
such that F|Ui = fi, we can identify H0(U, S) with the group S(X) of global
sections. Note that this is independent of the cover U.
Example 4.26. If $n = 1$ , $Z^1\left(\mathscr U, \sS \right)$ consists of sections $\la_{\iota j}$ satisfying
$d^1\la_{\iota j k} = \la_{jk} + \la_{\iota k} + \la_{\iota j} = 0$ in $\S\left( \sU_{\iota j k}\right)$. When the sheaf $\S$ is the sheaf of $\T$-
valued functions, we write everything multiplicatively, and the family $\la_{\iota j}: \sU_{\iota j} \to \T$ is a cocycle when
\be
\la_{\iota k} =\la_{\iota j} + \la_{ jk} \text{ on } U_{\iota jk} (4.6)
\ee
The cocycle $\left\{\la_{\iota j}\right\}$ is a coboundary when there are continuous functions $\mu_\iota : \sU_\iota \to \T$
such that
\be
\la_{\iota j}= \mu_\iota^{-1}\mu_j \quad \text{on} \quad \sU_{\iota j}
\ee

Before we launch into a detailed analysis of these cohomology groups, we pause
to show why they might be of interest to operator algebraists. Recall from Chapter 1
that every automorphism of the algebra K(H) of compact operators has the form
Ad u for some u ? U(H). For the algebra C0(T,K(H)), one might ask whether
an automorphism has the form Ad u for some continuous map u : T ? U(H).
Certainly not all will: each Ad u commutes with the natural action of C0(T) by
pointwise scalar multiplication, and not all automorphisms do this. (For example,
the automorphism f 7? f ? h induced by a nontrivial homeomorphism h of T does
not.) So we consider only automorphisms ? which preserve this C0(T)-module
structure: we write $\a \in \Aut_{C_0\left( T\right) }\left(T, \K\left( \H\right)  \right)$ . Now the question becomes really
interesting: there is a cohomology class $\zeta\left(\a \right)$  which is a \textit{complete
obstruction} to writing $\a = \mathrm{Ad}u$. This result will be substantially generalized in 
Theorem 5.42, where we will also prove that every class in H1(U, S) arises as some
?(?).
\begin{proposition}
	PAGE 75
Proposition 4.27. Suppose $T$ is a paracompact locally compact space, and $\a \in \Aut_{C_0\left( T\right) }\left(T, \K\left( \H\right)  \right)$. Let $\S$ denote the sheaf of germs of continuous $\T$-valued
functions on $T$. Then there is an open cover $\mathscr U$ of $T$ and a cocycle $\left\{\la_{\iota j}\right\} \in Z^1\left(\mathscr U, \S\right)$ whose class $\zeta\left(\a\right) = \left[\la_{\iota j}\right] \in Z^1\left(\mathscr U, \S\right)$ vanishes if and only if there is a
continuous function $u : T \to U\left(\H \right)$  satisfying
\bean
\forall t \in T \quad \forall f \in C_0\left( T, \K\left(\H \right) \right)\quad \a\left( f\right) \left( t\right) = u\left( t\right) f\left( t\right)u^* \left( t\right).
\eean 

\end{proposition}

\begin{empt} PAGE 109 !!!
We are now ready to define the Dixmier-Douady invariant of a bundle p : X ? Z
with fibre K(H) and structure group AutK(H) over a paracompact space Z. Choose
a family of local trivializations of p : X ? Z, and let ?ij : Uij ? AutK(H) be
the corresponding transition functions, which form a cocycle with coefficients in
the sheaf A of continuous AutK(H)-valued functions. By Remark 4.54, the bundle
is determined up to isomorphism by the class [?ij ] in H1(Z,A). By Lemma 4.83,
there is a class ([?ij ]) in H2(Z, S) which vanishes if and only if, after refinement
of the cover {Ui }, { ?ij } has the form Ad ??ij for some cocycle { ?ij } with values
in the sheaf U of continuous U(H)-valued functions. The Dixmier-Douady class
of the bundle p : X ? Z is the image ?(X) in H3(Z;Z) of ([?ij ]) under the
isomorphism H2(Z, S) ?= H3(Z;Z) of Theorem 4.42. We have essentially proved
the following version of the Dixmier-Douady Classification Theorem:

\end{empt}
\begin{theorem}
Theorem 4.85. !!! PAGE 109. Let H be a Hilbert space, and let p : X ? Z be a bundle over a
paracompact space Z with fibre K(H) and structure group AutK(H).
(a) The Dixmier-Douady class ?(X) vanishes if and only if the bundle has tran-
sition functions of the form Ad ??ij , for some open cover {Ui } of Z and
continuous functions ?ij : Uij ? U(H) satisfying ?ij?jk = ?ik on Uijk.
(b) If H is infinite-dimensional, the Dixmier-Douady class ?(X) determines p :
X ? Z up to isomorphism, and all classes in H3(Z;Z) arise as the Dixmier-
Douady class of some such bundle.
\end{theorem}
